894. Gelek peyv û gotin û zanyarî li ser Sîyamend hatine gotin.
894. Many sayings and words and information have been said about Sîyamend.

895. Hin dibêjin ew kurê Silêman Beg bû mîrê herêma Sîpanê û piştî bavê wî mir, ew zarok bû kete ber destê apê Selîm Beg de.
895. Some say he was the son of Silêman Beg, mîr of the region of Sîpan, and after his father died, he was a child and fell into the hand of his uncle Selîm Beg.

896. Çavreşî avêtinê heya apê wî berdayê ji malê û bû şivanê (serwanê) golika, pêxwas, tazî û bêkiras.
896. They cast black-eyes (jealousy/malice) upon him until his uncle dismissed him from the house and he became the shepherd (herdsman) of calves, barefoot, naked and shirtless.

897. Û hin dibêjin Sîyamend kurê amê Xecê bû, sêwî û feqîr bû, apê Xecê ew nedayê û da kurê mîrê Xursê û Sîyamend bi pey ketîye heya çend rojan, ew bi cih kirîye û revandîye.
897. And some say Sîyamend was the paternal cousin of Xecê, he was an orphan and poor, Xecê's uncle did not give her to him and gave her to the son of the mîr of Xurs, and Sîyamend went after her for a few days, located her and kidnapped her.

898. Û hin dibêjin Xecê qîza Omer Begê, mîrê Heranê ye, di biharî de derketîye koçerîyê, konê dozdehstûnî li Berîya Serhedê vegirtîye, êrîşek dijminan girtîye ser Omer beg, ew û her şeş lawên wî kuştine û Xecê revandine ji xwe re birine.
898. And some say Xecê is the daughter of Omer Beg, mîr of Heran, in the spring she went out to nomadism, pitched the twelve-pillared tent in the Plain of Serhed, an attack of enemies caught upon Omer Beg, they killed him and all six of his sons and kidnapped Xecê and took her for themselves.

899. Sîyamend û berkarê xwe Qeregêtran di wê hindamê re derbas dibin, dîtin kuştin û talanîya konê mezin li dar e û hewar û gazîya qîzê (Xecê) bi qîrîn û nalîn û girî tê, hema Sîyamend nemerdîyê nake û êrîşî van mêrkuj û talankeran dikir û birayê wî Qeregêtran pê re mêr kuştin û talan vegerandin û Xecê bi darê zorê ji wan stendin, paşê Sîyamend Xecê li xwe mehir dike.
899. Sîyamend and his servant Qeregêtran are passing by in that moment, they saw the killing and plundering of the great tent is ongoing and the cry and call of the girl (Xecê) comes with shouting and groaning and crying, Sîyamend just does not do ungenerosity (does not hesitate) and attacked these murderers and plunderers and his brother Qeregêtran with him killed men and returned the plunder and took Xecê from them by the stick of force, then Sîyamend marries Xecê to himself.

900. Û hin dibêjin Siyamend yekî sêwî û sewtere bû, kurê yekî feqîr bû, kete ber destê ap û amojina xwe de û ew xistine şivanê kehrika û gurîkê dar û devîya.
900. And some say Sîyamend was an orphan and an idle one, he was the son of a poor man, he fell under the hands of his uncle and aunt and they made him the shepherd of fawns and a scabby boy of trees and bushes.

901. Lê tiştê em dizanin û rast e ew ku Siyamend kurê yekî kurd e ji gundê (bajarê Silîvayê), nevîyê mêrxas û leheng û pehlewanan e, di demek zor û zehmet de hatiye dunyayê û gelekî jarî û mijûlî û tazî û birçîtî dîtîye.
901. But the thing we know and is true is that Sîyamend is the son of a Kurd from the village (the city of Silîva), he is the descendant of braves and heroes and champions, he has come to the world in a forceful and difficult time and has seen much misery and busyness (trouble) and nakedness and hunger.

902. Dibêjin gundîyên Siliva -wilo hatîye gotin- piştî şerê dijminan û êrîşkeran bi demeke dirêj, milet rawistîya û hedinî û kete bin zordarîya osmanîyan de.
902. They say the villagers of Silîva - so it has been said - after the war of enemies and attackers for a long time, the nation stopped and calmed down and fell under the oppression of the Ottomans.

903. Tu kes nema dikare serê xwe rake li dijî wan.
903. No one can anymore raise his head against them.

904. Miletê jar ê belengaz ji nû ve xwe dide hev û karê xwe dike.
904. The miserable and destitute nation gathers itself anew and does its work.

905. Kurd qenc zarokên xwe xwedî dikin, piştî kuştina zilam û mêrxasan bi hejmarên mezin û talanan, tiştek nehiştin ji malî û gundîyan re.
905. Kurds raise their children well, after the killing of men and braves in great numbers and plunders, they left nothing for the households and villagers.

906. Xelk ketin warekî reşîyê de bi şev û bi roj kar dikirin heya gepek nanê ceh ya parîk nanê garis bidin zarokên xwe û gelek ji gundîyan nanê ceh û garis bi dest wan nediket, gîya û rehik didan hev û tanîn dikelandin bi dew dikirin toraq û qawît û dixwarin, qurmê xerdelê (kurum) derdixistin û dikelandin û dixwarin.
906. The people fell into a state of blackness (misery), they were working by night and by day to give a bite of barley bread or a piece of millet bread to their children and many of the villagers, barley and millet bread would not fall into their hands, they would gather grass and roots and bring and boil them, with buttermilk they would make curd and qawît (roasted flour dish) and eat it, they would pull out mustard roots (kurum) and boil and eat them.

907. Kereng, gwîriz, tolik bi toraqê dikelandin û dixwarin.
907. They would boil thistles, gwîriz, mallow with curd and eat them.

908. Hey kua nanê ceh û firîk çêdibû xelkê bi dasa diçinî û feqra sinbil sinbil bi dû pala de ji xwe re didan hev û tanîn malê dikutan û dihêran û dixwarin.
908. Whenever barley bread and roasted green wheat would happen (be available), the people reaped with sickles and the poor gathered them ear by ear behind the reapers for themselves and brought them home, pounded and ground and ate them.

909. Dibêjin, piçekî halê gundîyan xweş bû gava cotkarî pey dakirin, çandinî kirin û pez û dewar xwedî kirin.
909. They say, the state of the villagers became a little pleasant when they pursued farming, did agriculture and raised sheep and cattle.

910. Pepûkê Sîyamend zarokek ji van zarokên gundîyan e, pêxwas û tazî û birçî û bêkiras e; sê çar salî bû bav mir û dê bi qerwaşî û nemalî û pars û pilûsê lawikê xwe xwedî dikir.
910. The poor Sîyamend is a child from these children of the villagers, he is barefoot and naked and hungry and shirtless; he was three or four years old when his father died and his mother with servitude and poverty and begging and pleading was raising her boy.

911. Ji birçîna, ji serma, pepûkê nexweş ket, ew jî mir, serê xwe danî çû ber dilovanîya Xwedê.
911. From hunger, from cold, the poor thing fell sick, she too died, she laid her head down and went before the mercy of God.

912. ## Siyamend li ber destê ap û amojinê
912. ## Sîyamend under the hand of the uncle and aunt

913. Sîyamendê biçûk û zarok temenê xwe şeş heft salî, sêwî bê dê û bê bav û ne kalikek (bapîr) û ne pîrik (dapîr).
913. Little and child Sîyamend, his age six or seven years old, an orphan without mother and without father and neither a grandfather nor a grandmother.

914. Pepûko kesî wî tune ye di gund de, ji apê wî Zerdo pê ve.
914. The poor boy, he has nobody in the village, other than his uncle Zerdo.

915. Apê reben û
915. The wretched and

916. feqîr bi zorê xwe û jina xwe têr nan û av dike û bêbaveke jina li cem wî bû.
916. poor uncle with difficulty satisfies himself and his wife with bread and water and there was a fatherless woman with him.

917. Zikreş, mûçtehl, zimançars, bibêje hema zebenîyeke, nahêle pepûkê Sîyamend parîk nan bixwe bi hesanî, û gotineke xweş tu cara ji devê wê dernayê û derneketîye.
917. Black-bellied (malicious), bitter-faced, coarse-tongued, say she is just a demon, she does not let poor Sîyamend eat a piece of bread easily, and a pleasant word never comes out of her mouth and has not come out.

918. Hema her jê re dibêje, "kuro Siyo gurîko here nav zarokan ji xwe re bilîz.
918. She just always says to him, "boy Siyo, you scabby boy, go among the children and play for yourself.

919. Kuro xwedênehişto ê weke te li ber kehir û berxa ne, ma ê min pepûka Xwedê çima şensê min wilo ye, Xwedê tu zarok nedan min û ez li gurî hesilîm!".
919. Boy, God-forsaken one, those like you are tending fawns and lambs, after all what of poor me of God, why is my luck like this, God did not give me any children and I am stuck with a scabby boy!".

920. Rebenê Sîyamand rojek ji rojên Xwedê xweşî nedît, jinapa wî ya bin navê Mirdê Xwedê ew ji rû xwe avêtîye, bêwijdan, zikreş û dilkevir e, carekê ji bo Xwedê rehm û dilovanî neket dilê wê de, ku hema firek av li serê vî sêwî bike û laşê wî û cilê wî bişo.
920. Wretched Sîyamend did not see pleasantness one day of God's days, his uncle's wife by the name of Merdê, God has thrown her from His face, she is conscienceless, black-bellied (malicious) and stone-hearted, not once for God did mercy and compassion fall into her heart, that she might just put a splash of water on this orphan's head and wash his body and his clothes.

921. Pepûko zarok e ji qilêr û xwêdanê, serî û laş û kinc tijî spî bûne; spîyan hêlînên xwe di serê wî de çêkirine, tijî nûtik û rişk kirine, pepûko hingî bi neynûkan dixurîne çermê serê wî kul dibû û xwîn jê dihat.
921. The poor boy is a child, from dirt and sweat, his head and body and clothes have become full of lice; the lice have made their nests in his head, have filled it with nits and eggs, the poor boy from scratching so much with his fingernails, the skin of his head would become a wound and blood would come from it.

922. Û ji vî halê qilêr û spî û xwêdan pepûko gurî bû û serê wî tijî kenik bû û navê wî ma Gurî di malê de, li nav zarokan, li nav gund û êl û eşîrê.
922. And from this state of dirt and lice and sweat the poor boy became scabby and his head became full of sores and his name remained Gurî (Scabby) in the house, among the children, among the village and tribe and clan.

923. Gurîyê reben li ber destê jinapa bêbav, parîk nan nade dest, carina xwarin marina ji ber apê wî dimîne datîne ber Gurî, hema pê qût dibe, li ser cilekê wek kurtan tijî pûş e radizê, bê lihêf e, ebak qetîyayî, peritî bi ser xwe de dadike li devê derîyê axurê gayê cot, û gurîyê birçî û tazî û pêxwas di nav zarokên gund de ji xwe re dilîst.
923. Wretched Gurî under the hand of the fatherless uncle's wife, she does not give a piece of bread to his hand, sometimes food and such remains from his uncle, she puts it before Gurî, he just sustains himself with it, he sleeps on a rug like a packsaddle full of straw, he is without a quilt, a torn, tattered cloak he pulls over himself at the mouth of the door of the plowing ox's stable, and hungry and naked and barefoot Gurî played for himself among the children of the village.

924. Carê gepek nan ji destê hinekan direvand û dixwar.
924. At times he would snatch a bite of bread from the hands of some and eat it.

925. Ji nêza berê xwe dida bixêrîka tenûra qene hinek parîk nan, gepek xwarin bidinê.
925. Out of hunger he would turn his direction to the charity-givers of the ovens so that perhaps some would give him a piece of bread, a bite of food.

926. Û bi vî halî jiyana xwe berdewam dikir, zikekî têr û dehê birçî, heya bû neh deh salî û destê wî dar girt û bû sîpanekî bi nav û deng û çeleng.
926. And in this state he continued his life, one belly full and ten hungry, until he became nine or ten years old and his hand held a stick and he became a renowned and famous and handsome youth.

927. Xortên di temanê wî de û mezintir jî xwe jê diparastin û jê ditirsîyan û nema ji tiştekî ditirsîya û xwe ji kesekî re danexist û xwe kêm nedikir û navê Gurî belav bû bi lehengî û pêlewanî û çelengi.
927. The youths in his age and older too protected themselves from him and feared him and he no longer feared anything and did not lower himself to anyone and did not diminish himself and Gurî's name spread with heroism and championship and handsomeness.

928. Di lîskên kaban de kesekî
928. In the games of knucklebones no one

929. zora wî nedibir û tim kabên zarokan ji wan dibir, kêm cara kab jê diçûn.
929. could defeat him and he always took the children's knucklebones from them, few times did knucklebones go from him (did he lose).

930. Lisken kaban ji kevin de di nav kurdan de hene û pê dilîstin.
930. Games of knucklebones exist from ancient times among the Kurds and they played with them.

931. Zarok û xort û heya zilaman bi Zikê Cûgê dilîstin û tişt ji hev distandin.
931. Children and youths and even up to men played Zikê Cûgê (a specific game) and took things from each other.

932. Lîskên kaban gelek in, ji wan lîskan: (Xîzê, kelê, sîrê, qulaptê, zikê).
932. The games of knucklebones are many, from those games: (Xîzê, kelê, sîrê, qulaptê, zikê).

933. Icar Gurî geh dilîst û geh diçû alîkarîya apê xwe û namê wî jê re dibir çolê ber cot û çêrandina gayê cot, û Gurî bixwe şivantîya kehir û berxan dikir li çolê û dûre bû gavanê golikan.
933. Now Gurî sometimes played and sometimes went to the help of his uncle and took his food to him in the wilderness before the plow and grazed the plowing ox, and Gurî himself did the shepherding of fawns and lambs in the wilderness and later became the herdsman of calves.

934. Dem bûye bihar, gundîyan dest bi cotê kirêba kirine û erdê şûv dajon bi cot.
934. The time has become spring, the villagers have started the plowing of fallow fields and plow the stubble land with the plow.

935. Dugîsin, sêgîsin dikin ji bo werzên (bistanên) şabeş, talikan (gundor) û icûr û tirozîyan biçînin.
935. They do two-plowshares, three-plowshares in order to plant fields (gardens) of watermelons, melons (cantaloupes) and cucumbers and snake cucumbers.

936. Serê sibê zû cotkaran bi serê gayê xwe digirtin û berê xwe didan nav erdên xwe û nîrên ser pişta hustê ga bi mijana halet ve bi qayîşê girê didan û dest bi cot dikirin, xet bi xet ji serê sersedê vedigerîyan.
936. Early in the morning the farmers took the head of their ox and turned their direction into their lands and tied the yokes on the back of the ox's neck to the pole of the plow with a strap and started plowing, line by line they returned from the head of the end of the field.

937. Apê Gurî jî Zerdo wek her car bi gundîyan re çûye cotê kirêba, ro hilatîye, taştîya wî hê nehatîye, Merdê (jinapa Gurî) di xew de maye.
937. Gurî's uncle Zerdo too as always has gone with the villagers to the plowing of fallow fields, the sun has risen, his breakfast has not yet come, Merdê (Gurî's uncle's wife) has remained in sleep.

938. Li malê çavên xwe vekirin, heydêê!
938. At home she opened her eyes, heydee!

939. Ro du bejnan bilind bûye, bi lez û bez beroşa nîskê vala kir elbekê û qelpaxa wê danî ser devê elbê û pêçeka nanê sêlê danî ser û bang kir Gurî û got: "Hêêêê!
939. The sun has risen two heights, with speed and running she emptied the pot of lentils into a wooden bowl and put its lid on the mouth of the bowl and placed the wrap of flatbread on top and called Gurî and said: "Heeee!

940. Gurîyo, çepelo, mêrdalo, qesifyo, apê te mir ji nêza li çolê".
940. Gurî, filthy one, dead-born one, cursed one, your uncle has died from hunger in the wilderness".

941. Amojina wî elba şorbê û pêçeka nanê sêlê sipartê û Gurî da ser rê.
941. His aunt entrusted the bowl of soup and the wrap of flatbread to him and Gurî set on the road.

942. Gavaku berê xwe da çolê cem cotê apê xwe, dît ku zarok bi kaba dilîzin, Gurî ji xwe re got: "Tew li min li min felekê, mala min çû bû mîratêêê.
942. As soon as he turned his direction to the wilderness to his uncle's plow, he saw that the children are playing with knucklebones, Gurî said to himself: "Woe to me to me fate, my house has gone to ruin.

943. Şevê çûnî kabek ji min çû, xew neketîye çavên min".
943. The past night one knucklebone went from me (I lost one), sleep has not entered my eyes".

944. Guri nigekî wî li hundir bû, yek li hewşê bû.
944. Gurî, one of his feet was inside, one was in the courtyard.

945. Di ber xwe de digot: "Li min xistîye fecra sibê û ez vegerînim kaba xwe li darê dinê".
945. He was saying to himself: "The dawn of the morning has struck upon me (it has dawned) and I will return my knucklebone in the world".

946. Li wê navê danî elba şorbê û bi ser dakir pêçeka nanê sêlê, û bi lez vegerîya malê kundirê kaba ji orta dîwêr û kewarê derxist.
946. At that place he placed the bowl of soup and put the wrap of flatbread over it, and with speed he returned home, he took out the gourd of knucklebones from the middle of the wall and the grain bin.

947. Gurî di gava bi zarokan re dilîze, û çawa Gurî kabê xwe diavêje jê re mîrkutek tê.
947. Gurî at the moment plays with the children, and how Gurî throws his knucklebone, a pestle (a heavy blow) comes for him.

948. "Hêêê... Gurî narî bû ku jinapa wî lê daye darê ber tifikê (sêlê) yoyo....
948. "Heee... Gurî had not gone when his uncle's wife struck him with the stick of before the hearth (flatbread griddle) yoyo....

949. Gurî ji ber jinapa xwe Merdê teloq bû, ji tirsa darê di destê wê".
949. Gurî fled from before his uncle's wife Merdê, from the fear of the stick in her hand."

950. Merdê bang kirîyê, “Gurîyo, çepelo, mirdalo, xwedênehişto, apê te mir ji nêza li çolê, û hîn tu bi kaba dilîzî li vê gasînê?"
950. Merdê called to him, "Gurî, filthy one, dead-born one, God-forsaken one, your uncle died from hunger in the wilderness, and still you play with knucklebones in this square?"

951. Hema Gurî rahişt kundirê kaba û siparte jinapê û rahişt pêçeka nanê sêlê û elba şorbê û berê xwe da cotê apê xwe.
951. Just then Gurî picked up the gourd of knucklebones and entrusted it to his uncle's wife and picked up the wrap of flatbread and the bowl of soup and turned his direction to his uncle's plow.

952. Li çolê hooo.. hoy, di gava Gurî berê xwe da çolê, newalek kete pêşîyê de.
952. In the wilderness hooo.. hoy, in the moment Gurî turned his direction to the wilderness, a valley fell before him.

953. Newaleke kûr û dirêj bû, Gurî li hawîrdora xwe nerî tu kes nexuya ye ji Xwedê pê ve, ezmaneke bilind û erdeke vala ye, li wê navê danîbû elba şorbê, pêçeka nanê sêlê, bi carekê re çandîyê.
953. It was a deep and long valley, Gurî looked around his surroundings no one is visible other than God, it is a high sky and an empty land, at that place he had placed the bowl of soup, the wrap of flatbread, all at once he planted it (set to eating it).

954. Gurî got: "Hêêê... tew li min felekê, ay xayinê ez xistibûm ber lepê ap û amojinê, hisreta min bû ez carekê têr bixwim nanê sêlê.
954. Gurî said: "Heee... woe to me fate, oh traitor you had put me before the palm of my uncle and aunt, it was my longing that I eat flatbread to satisfaction once.

955. Îro ez ê xelas bikim vê elba şorbê û pêçeka nanê sêlê".
955. Today I will finish this bowl of soup and the wrap of flatbread".

956. Û bi qutekevçîya hatibû şorba nîskê, û leyvanê şorbê, û parîk nan nehiştibû li binê elbê, û ji ber xwe derxistibû çîplaqê devê, û ji jêr de lê xistibû li binê bêxwedîya elbê.
956. And with wooden spoons he had come to the lentil soup, and licked the soup, and had not left a piece of bread at the bottom of the bowl, and from his side he had taken out the sharp dagger, and from below he had struck it at the bottom of the ownerless bowl.

957. Gurî têr xwar û pişta xwe rast kir û berê xwe da cotê apê xwe.
957. Gurî ate to satisfaction and straightened his back and turned his direction to his uncle's plow.

958. Tenatena dimeşîya nola bajarîya, destê xwe dabû pişta xwe li meşê.
958. He was walking leisurely like city folk, he had put his hand on his back in walking.

959. Çavên apê wî li devê rêya wî qerimî bûn, ji birçîna westîyabû bi dû cotê ga de.
959. His uncle's eyes were frozen at the mouth of his road, from hunger he had tired behind the plow of the ox.

960. Wa nerî ku Gurî tenatena dimeşe û bi rê de tê û hayê wî ji bayê felekê tune ye.
960. There he looked that Gurî walks leisurely and comes on the road and he has no awareness of the wind of fate.

961. Apê birçî ji hêrs û qehra di dilê xwe de got: "Bera te çikiribe Gurî, ku ez te bigirim".
961. The hungry uncle from the anger and wrath in his heart said: "Let whatever you have done Gurî, when I catch you".

962. Apê Zerdo zane ku ne bi fenekî be Gurî nayê girtin û zeftkirin.
962. Uncle Zerdo knows that if not with a trick Gurî will not be caught and captured.

963. Rabû li ser serê xwe di xeta cot de rabidand, xwe kire pîj.
963. He got up and stretched out on his head in the plow line, he made himself stiff.

964. Gurî di ser re sekinî û got: Apo te xêr e?
964. Gurî stopped above him and said: Uncle is it well with you?

965. Apê Zerdo: Law wele ez ketime tayê.
965. Uncle Zerdo: Boy by God I have fallen into a fever.

966. Gurî: Hê mala min çû mîratê.
966. Gurî: Heh my house has gone to ruin.

967. (Û bi ser de daqûl hat).
967. (And he bent over him).

968. Dema xwe daqûl kir, apê Zerdo xwe zer kirîyê û bi damara qirikê girt.
968. When he bent himself, Uncle Zerdo lunged at him and grabbed by the vein of the throat.

969. Hê apê girtibû bi damara qirikê û bi misasa daweşandê.
969. Just as the uncle had grabbed by the vein of the throat and struck him with the ox-goad.

970. Hê ji bîst û pênc misasa, Gurî nehişt bigihîyê.
970. Even from twenty and five goads, Gurî did not let it reach him.

971. Gurî wek pêlewana xwe ji nav lepê apê xwe filitand û revîya li çolê, û got: "Bi qirara qesem (bi sûnd û peyman) li can û cesedê min ketibe. heya yek xerab hebe, ez nakim yekê”.
971. Gurî like champions escaped himself from among his uncle's palm and fled in the wilderness, and said: "May the decision of the oath (with oath and pact) have fallen on my soul and body. as long as one bad exists, I will not do one (good)".

972. Û Gurî bi dizî li apê xwe vegerîya û jê dizî gayê sor, gayê bedêlê, û berê xwe da malê û dibêje, "çiqas xera bûn li bejn û balê.
972. And Gurî stealthily returned to his uncle and stole from him the red ox, the substitute ox, and turned his direction to home and says, "how many ruins (calamities) were upon the stature and figure.

973. Û ji îro pêve heya a xerab hebe, ez nema dikim a qenc".
973. And from today onward as long as the bad exists, I no longer do the good".

974. Guri gayê çavsor ajot malê û bang kir jinapa xwe:
974. Gurî drove the red-eyed ox home and called his uncle's wife:

975. "Ho jinapê! Apê min gelek silava li te dike û dibêje, gayê çavsor şer jê kin û xanîyê biçûk xera bikin, bikin ard û têxin bin".
975. "Ho uncle's wife! My uncle makes many greetings to you and says, slaughter the red-eyed ox and ruin the small house, make it firewood and put it under (the pot)".

976. Merdê: Xêre law Gurî?
976. Merdê: Is it well boy Gurî?

977. Çima çi qewimîye?
977. Why what has happened?

978. Gurî: Apê min dibêje, şeva çûyî min xewnek dît, hê ez sax im, ez ê xêra xwe û a dê û bavê xwe bidim.
978. Gurî: My uncle says, last night I saw a dream, while I am still alive, I will give my charity and that of my mother and father.

979. Merdê: Law wele min jî şevê dî xewnek dîtibû bi vî zikî ez du lawa tînem, lê min ji apê te re negot, min go, ez pîrek im, ji min bawer nake.
979. Merdê: Boy by God I too had seen a dream last night that with this belly I bring two boys, but I did not tell your uncle, I said, I am a woman, he will not believe me.

980. De ban çend xorta bik û ga zû bavêj erdê, hê sibe ye, incex çêbibe şîvê.
980. Then call a few youths and throw the ox to the ground quickly, it is still morning, it will barely be ready for dinner.

981. Guri rabû bi lez û bez çend xortên serserî nala xwe civandin û ga avêtin erdê û serî jê kirin û zû çerm bi ser de anîn û hûr kirin, xistin niqrîyê (beroşa mezin) û beroş sipartin hev, û heşt û mirdîyaqên kadinê kirin ardû û dan bin berosa.
981. Gurî got up with speed and running gathered a few idle youths like himself and they threw the ox to the ground and cut its head and quickly brought the skin over it (skinned it) and chopped it, put it into the niqrî (large pot) and stacked the pots together, and they made the roof beams and posts of the barn firewood and put them under the pots.

982. agir gur kirin û bû pelq pelqa goştê gê.
982. they stoked the fire and it became the bubbling of the ox's meat.

983. Hêê, gelekî kêfa Gurî tê, Gurî rahiştibû heskê û li hev dixe goştê gê û dibêje, "şabaş ji Xwedê re ku ez xistibûm ber lepê ap û amojinê de û îro ez ê têr bixwim goştê gê, li min li min hayoyo".
983. Heee, Gurî's joy comes very much, Gurî had picked up the ladle and stirs the ox's meat and says, "bravo to God that He had put me before the palm of the uncle and aunt and today I will eat the ox's meat to satisfaction, woe to me to me hayoyo".

984. Û Gurî carina berê xwe dide alîyê malê radihêje pêçeka nanê sêlê û dixe nav avdonka gê, dixe legenê û bi heskê lê dike avdonka gê.
984. And Gurî sometimes turns his direction to the side of the house picks up the wrap of flatbread and puts it into the broth of the ox, puts it into the basin and with the ladle pours the ox's broth upon it.

985. Gava ku Gurî dixwe bi xwarinê re vê dibêje, "spas ji Xwedê re gava ez xistibûm ber lepê ap û amojinê de, mane hisreta gurî bû ku têr bixwe avdonka gê, li min hayo".
985. When Gurî eats with the food he says this, "thanks to God when He had put me before the palm of the uncle and aunt, for it was Gurî's longing that he eats the ox's broth to satisfaction, woe to me hayo".

986. Xort û nasî û zarok, kom bûne li hewşa Zerdo û pîrek û zilam tên dipirsin, "ha Merdîya xêr e?
986. Youths and acquaintances and children, have gathered in Zerdo's courtyard and women and men come ask, "ah Merdîya is it well?

987. Ev çi ye?
987. What is this?

988. We çi bihîstîye?"
988. What have you heard?"

989. Merdîya: Xêr e, xêr e îşeleh.
989. Merdîya: It is well, it is well God willing.

990. Wele şevê dî Zerdo xewnek dîtîye û dixwaze bi saxî xêrekê li xwe û dê û bavê xwe bide.
990. By God last night Zerdo saw a dream and wants to give a charity for himself and his mother and father while alive.

991. Pîrek û cînar: De ser xêrê be, Xwedê qebûl bike.
991. Women and neighbors: Then let it be on goodness, may God accept it.

992. Şerîfa: Pepû welê, qey xalê Zerdo hîn xêra dê û bavê xwe nedaye?!
992. Şerîfa: Oh dear is that so, has Uncle Zerdo not given the charity of his mother and father yet?!

993. Merdîya: Mane em wê çaxê feqîr bûn, çî me hebû em xêra bidin.
993. Merdîya: For we were poor at that time, what did we have that we should give charities.

994. Fato: De ser xêrê be law, belkî Xwedê li we bê rehmê û bedena te şîn bike.
994. Fato: Then let it be on goodness child, perhaps God will come to mercy on you and make your body green (bless you with a child).

995. Merdîya: Hûû.. xaltîka Fato, mane min jî şeva çûyî xewnek dîtibû.
995. Merdîya: Hooo.. Aunt Fato, for I too had seen a dream last night.

996. Fato: Xêr e keça min, îşeleh xêr e?
996. Fato: Is it well my daughter, God willing it is well?

997. Merdîya: Xêr e, xêr e îşeleh.
997. Merdîya: It is well, it is well God willing.

998. Min dît bi vî zikî ez du lawa tînim (û dengê xwe nizim kir, qene dengê wê nerê kesekî, û jin û pîrekê gund wê çavînokî nekin, çav hene û gelek dilbijok jî hene).
998. I saw with this belly I bring two boys (and she lowered her voice, so that her voice would not reach anyone, and the women and females of the village would not cast the evil eye on her, there are eyes and there are many envious ones too).

999. Fato: De his law, dengê xwe neke û hilîne, jin û pîrekên gundê Silîva dilbijok in, çavbirçîn e.
999. Fato: Then hush child, do not make your voice and put it away, the women and females of the village of Silîva are envious, they are hungry-eyed.

1000. Merdîya: Xaltîka Fatma, ji te hinek goşt û avdonk (û bi heskê xiste firaxekê de) û dibêje, "bera zarok bixwin, mane xêr".
1000. Merdîya: Aunt Fatma, for you some meat and broth (and with the ladle she put it into a dish) and says, "let the children eat, for it is charity".

1001. xaltîka Fato tasa goştî xiste bin pêşmalka xwe de û dibêje, "Xwedê kurekî salih bide te, Xwedê xêra we qebûl bike".
1001. Aunt Fato put the bowl of meat under her apron and says, "May God give you a righteous son, may God accept your charity".

1002. Çîçekê ji Sînemê re got: Rebenê va belengaza gayê bedêlê gurandine, ji ber xewnekê!
1002. Çîçek said to Sînem: Wretched one look these destitutes have slaughtered the substitute ox, because of a dream!

1003. Sînemê: Yadê şensê xelkê heye, mêrê wan ji wan bawer dikin.
1003. Sînem: Mother the people have luck, their husbands believe them.

1004. Çiçek: Çima?
1004. Çîçek: Why?

1005. Ma te jî tu xewn dîtine ku bi zikekî tu du lawa bînî?
1005. After all have you too seen any dreams that with one belly you bring two boys?

1006. Sînem: Na wele min tu xewnên wilo nedîtine, lê hema şensê hina erdê vediqelêşe!
1006. Sînem: No by God I have not seen any such dreams, but simply the luck of some cleaves the earth!

1007. Gundî Hêdî hêdî, zilam, zarok û pîrek tên bi alîyê mala Zerdoyî de û dipirsin ka bê çi çêbûye.
1007. The villagers slowly, men, children and women come to the side of Zerdo's house and ask to see what has happened.

1008. Agir û dûman û tencerîyên li ser keviran.
1008. Fire and smoke and pots on the stones.

1009. Gundi gosretmayî mane, Zerdo feqîr e, çima wê gayê xwe şer jê bike?
1009. The villagers have remained astounded, Zerdo is poor, why would he slaughter his ox?

1010. Û Gurî hayê wî ji kesî tune ye, carê dire çend nana tîne û dixîne leganê û bi heskê avdonka gê lê dike û bi qutekevçîya diavêjê devê xwe û dixwe û dibêje, "îro ez ê têr bixwim, ji nanê sêlê û avdonkê gê".
1010. And Gurî, his awareness is of no one, at times he goes brings a few breads and puts them into the basin and with the ladle pours the ox's broth on it and with wooden spoons throws it into his mouth and eats and says, "today I will eat to satisfaction, from the flatbread and the ox's broth".

1011. Belengazê Zerdo ji tîna û birçîna cotê xwe temam nekir û seda xwe nîvco hişt.
1011. Destitute Zerdo from thirst and hunger did not complete his plowing and left his field unfinished.

1012. Qarîşa mijanê vekir û bi rişma her du gayan di bin nîr de girt û berê xwe da malê.
1012. He opened the strap of the plow-pole and held by the halter of both oxen under the yoke and turned his direction to home.

1013. Bi ser çavê pêşîya gund ket, heydê!
1013. He fell upon the front face of the village, heydee!

1014. Qîr û qîyamet li Hewşa wî ye, got: "Ya Rebî stara te, ev çi bela hatîye ser mala me?
1014. Crying and resurrection (chaos) is in his courtyard, he said: "O Lord your protection, what is this calamity that has come upon our house?

1015. Ya Rebî tu xêr bikî".
1015. O Lord may you do good (make it well)".

1016. Ji tirsa û ji qehr û kerba lezand û bi zixtê niquçand gayan, ku zû bimeşin.
1016. From fear and from wrath and anger he sped up and poked the oxen with the goad, that they might walk quickly.

1017. Zerdo gihaşt nav gund, gundî, zilam û jin û zarok hemû jê re dibêjin, "Xwedê xêr bike xewna te û Xwedê xêra we qebûl bike, Xwedê bi ber destê mirîyan ve bigihîne".
1017. Zerdo reached inside the village, the villagers, men and women and children all say to him, "May God make your dream good and may God accept your charity, may God make it reach before the hands of the dead".

1018. Zarok: Xalê Zerdo Xwedê qebûl bike, goştê gayê sor xweş bû.
1018. Children: Uncle Zerdo may God accept it, the meat of the red ox was pleasant.

1019. Zerdo: Goştê gayê sor çi ye kuro?
1019. Zerdo: What meat of the red ox boy?

1020. Hûn çi dibêjin?!
1020. What are you saying?!

1021. Zarok: Wey xalo mane Gurî gayê sor ser jê kir û digot: "Xêra dê û bavê apê min e".
1021. Children: Woe uncle for Gurî slaughtered the red ox and was saying: "It is the charity of my uncle's mother and father".

1022. Zerdo: Wey emirquto, xwedênehişto, ma ez te bigirim hey vanê rih bi te ve bernadim.
1022. Zerdo: Woe you short-lifed one, God-forsaken one, if I catch you I will just not leave a soul attached to you.

1023. Û lezand berê xwe da malê û di dilê xwe de dibêje, "ma ez ê te negirim Guri".
1023. And he sped up and turned his direction to home and in his heart he says, "will I not catch you Gurî".

1024. Gihaşt hewşê hêê, rê û rêwanî tune ye
1024. He reached the courtyard hee, there is no road and passage

1025. ji gundîyan, bêhna goşt kirine.
1025. from the villagers, they have smelled the meat.

1026. Zilam, jin, pîrek û zarok giş dibêjin, "Xwedê qebûl bike xêra we, xalê Zerdo".
1026. Men, women, females and children all say, "May God accept your charity, Uncle Zerdo".

1027. Zerdo guh nade kesekî û çav di serî de sor bûne ji qehra bersiva kesekî nade û hema çavê xwe li Gurî diqelizîne û di nav gundîya û cînara re xwe dizîvirîne bi dizî, dixwaze xwe bigihîne Gurî, nas kirîye ku bela wî ji Gurî ye.
1027. Zerdo gives ear to no one and the eyes in his head have become red from wrath he does not give an answer to anyone and just darts his eyes at Gurî and among the villagers and neighbors turns himself stealthily, he wants to reach Gurî, he has recognized that his calamity is from Gurî.

1028. Merdîya hat pêşîyê, bi serê gayê dibin nîr de girt û got: "Zerdo tu sûcê min tune ye, birazîyê te Gurî, bi serê gê girtibû û hat got: “Apê min gotîye ser jê bike ez ê xêra dê û bavê xwe bidim hîn ez sax im, ma ez pepûka Xwedê çi di destê min de heye, ma ez karim bi Gurî?"
1028. Merdîya came before him, held by the head of the ox under the yoke and said: "Zerdo there is no crime of mine, your nephew Gurî, had held by the head of the ox and came and said: 'My uncle has said slaughter it I will give the charity of my mother and father while I am still alive', after all what does poor me of God have in my hand, after all can I deal with Gurî?"

1029. Zerdo: Bera te çi kiribe Gurî ku ez te bigirim.
1029. Zerdo: Let whatever you have done Gurî when I catch you.

1030. (Û meşîya ber bi Gurî de).
1030. (And he walked towards Gurî).

1031. Gurî nas kir ku apê wî bi alîyê wî de tê û hema erdê jê didize; hema rahişt çiplaqê xwe yê devê û xwe ji nav gundîyan da alîyekî û revîya.
1031. Gurî recognized that his uncle comes to his side and just steals the ground from him (sneaks up); he just picked up his sharp dagger and put himself aside from among the villagers and fled.

1032. Zerdo: Kuro bi dû kevin, wî ji min re bigirin.
1032. Zerdo: Boys fall behind him, catch him for me.

1033. (Sîpe û zarokan bera dû dan).
1033. (The youths and children went after him).

1034. Gurî di wa vegerîya û got: "Kuro vegerin ez ê li we xim", û çend kevir avêtin wan, zarok ji ber telaq bûn û ji tirsa bi şûnde vegerîyan.
1034. Gurî returned upon them and said: "Boys return I will strike you", and he threw a few stones at them, the children broke away from before him and from fear returned back.

1035. Pepûkê apê da dû, lê wê çi bike, nedigihayê û ne dikare bi dû bikeve.
1035. The poor uncle went after, but what will he do, he was not reaching him and cannot fall behind (keep up).

1036. Bi şûnde vegerîya malê, dikulkule ji qehra, ji birçîna, ji westandina cot, piştxûz bûye û bû niç niça wî bi xwe re dipeyive weke dîna lê hatîye.
1036. He returned back home, he boils from wrath, from hunger, from the fatigue of the plow, he has become hunchbacked and it became his muttering speaking with himself as if madness had come upon him.

1037. Gurî jî revîya bi qelaça ket bû çete û rêbir di çîyayên dora gundê Silîva de, nema dihêle ne yek ji gund derkeve û ne yek were gund, û dest bi xerabîya kir: Guhê kera jê dike, terîya çêleka qut dike, guhanê bizina diçirîne, li şivana dide, çiplaqê devê wa vedigerîne malê nav gund û werz û reza, darê mêwa û fêkî berebat dike, radike û diçine û davê erdê.
1037. Gurî too fled, fell to the peaks and became a bandit and highwayman in the mountains around the village of Silîva, he no longer lets neither one go out of the village nor one come to the village, and he started bad deeds: he cuts off the ears of donkeys, cuts the tails of cows, tears the udders of goats, strikes the shepherds, with sharp daggers he turns them back home inside the village and fields and vineyards, desolates the trees of vines and fruits, plucks and picks them and throws them to the ground.

1038. Gundîyên Silîvayê ji ber ketine qelaqê, dengê Gurî bela bû li şar û gunda, li çarçîya, çîrok û serpêhatîyê gundîyan mane
1038. The villagers of Silîva because of him have fallen into agitation, Gurî's voice spread in the cities and villages, in the markets, the stories and adventures of the villagers have remained

1039. li ser Gurî û finasê ku dike.
1039. upon Gurî and the trickery that he does.

1040. Demek derbas bû, gundî û Gurî bi vî hali ne.
1040. A time passed, the villagers and Gurî are in this state.

1041. Dibêjin rojekê ji rojan, rokê daye serê Gurî kenê xwe dixurîne, çû li bin darekê rûnişt û xilmaş bû.
1041. They say one day of the days, the sun had struck Gurî's head, he scratches his sores, he went and sat under a tree and dozed off.

1042. Siwarek ji wir de tê hayê wî ji vê bazarê tune ye, mêrik xort e dil bi xwe ve ye, qîzek ji gund ji xwe re xwestibû, wê bê Silîva serdana malbava dergîsîyê, di ser Gurî re sekinî û deng lê kir, "kuro Guriyo tu li vir çi dikî?"
1042. A rider comes from there, he has no awareness of this market (affair), the man is a youth and pleased with himself, he had asked for a girl from the village for himself, he will come to Silîva to visit the father's house of the fiancée, he stopped above Gurî and called to him, "boy Gurî what are you doing here?"

1043. Gurî xilmaş e û çavlixew e bi hêdî got: "Wele ji xwe ez li vir im".
1043. Gurî is dozing and his eyes are in sleep he slowly said: "By God well I am here".

1044. Siwar dev jê berda û berê xwe da gund mala xezûrê xwe.
1044. The rider gave up on him and turned his direction to the village to his father-in-law's house.

1045. Êvarî piştî gundî şîvê dixwin, berê xwe didin odeya gund, şevbihêrkê.
1045. In the evening after the villagers eat dinner, they turn their direction to the village room, for the evening gathering.

1046. Şevbihêrka gundîyan giş li ser Gurî û finasên Gurî derbas bû û gişa berê xwe daye apê Gurî û jê re dibêjin, "wele em nema wilo ji te qebûl dikin".
1046. The evening gathering of the villagers entirely passed upon Gurî and Gurî's trickery and all turned their direction to Gurî's uncle and say to him, "by God we no longer accept it like this from you".

1047. Ê dibêje, birazîyê te îro terîya çêleka me jê kirîye, û hin dibêjin, îro Gurî guhanê bizina me çirandîye û ê dibêje, guhê kera me jê kirîye, û ê dibêje, wele Gurî darê mêwê me giş şikandibûn û tirî berebat kiribû.
1047. One says, your nephew today cut off the tail of our cow, and some say, today Gurî tore the udder of our goat and one says, he cut off the ear of our donkey, and one says, by God Gurî had broken all our vine trees and desolated the grapes.

1048. Bi vî rengî her yek ji xwe re tiştekî dibêje û apê reben nikare bersiva yekî bide.
1048. In this manner each says something to himself and the wretched uncle cannot give an answer to anyone.

1049. Ji hêrs û qehra got: "De hema giş rabin alîkarîya min bikin, em ê wî bigirin û ez ê wî qeyd û bend bikim bi zincîrê û bavêjim axur, de werin....haa.....
1049. From anger and wrath he said: "Then let all just rise and do my help, we will catch him and I will fetter and bind him with the chain and throw him in the stable, come on then.... haa.....

1050. ne hûn nayên, hûn derewa dikin, kes newêre xwe tê derxe".
1050. no you do not come, you make lies, no one dares to extract himself into it (interfere)".

1051. Civat: Yabo birazîyê te ye û ji te tê xwestin.
1051. The gathering: Father, he is your nephew and he is wanted from you (you are responsible for him).

1052. Simo: Em ê çima xwe têxin werta Gurî de, biner bê zarokên me nakuje?
1052. Simo: Why will we put ourselves into the middle of Gurî, look if he won't kill our children?

1053. Silo: Kî kare bi Gurî lawo?!
1053. Silo: Who can deal with Gurî boy?!

1054. Bi Xwedê çîplaqekî li kê xe nahêle av bigihê ser.
1054. By God whoever he strikes a sharp dagger upon he does not let water reach his head (he will kill him instantly).

1055. Şero: Çima?
1055. Şero: Why?

1056. Wele ku em giş xwe lê bikin yek, em ê pê karibin.
1056. By God if we all make ourselves one upon him, we will be able to deal with him.

1057. Bizdo: Weh çawa!
1057. Bizdo: Woe how!

1058. Hûn ê pê karibin, bi Xwedê wê bîsta bikuje heya hûn wî bigirin û yan negirin û belkî bireve bi serê çîya keve, wele tajî jî nagihênê.
1058. You will be able to deal with him, by God he will kill twenty until you catch him or do not catch him and perhaps he will flee and fall to the peak of the mountain, by God even a greyhound will not reach him.

1059. Şerîfo: Êê...soxî!
1059. Şerîfo: Eee... finally!

1060. De ka em çi bikin?
1060. Then come what shall we do?

1061. Çarakê em jêr bibînin.
1061. Let us find a remedy for it.

1062. Zerdo apê Gurî: Ka em ê xefkê rovîya û gura li ber vedin.
1062. Zerdo, Gurî's uncle: Well we will set traps of foxes and wolves before him.

1063. Silêmano: Ha hew, çima Gurî kor e, bêçav e, xefka nas nake, xefk nedîtine?
1063. Silêmano: Hah enough, why is Gurî blind, without eyes, does he not recognize traps, has he not seen traps?

1064. Şêro: de ka em ê bi şev lê biqelizin, belkî em wî di xew de bigirin.
1064. Şêro: then well we will sneak upon him by night, perhaps we might catch him in sleep.

1065. Zerdo: Kuro ma Gurî kengî radizê, çavên wî wek ê kîvroşkê ne, tim vekirî ne.
1065. Zerdo: Boy after all when does Gurî sleep, his eyes are like those of a rabbit, they are always open.

1066. Civatê şev dirêj kir û tiştek ji hev fêm nekirin, û tu çare nedîtin.
1066. The gathering extended the night and understood nothing from each other, and they saw no remedy.

1067. Di civatê de xortê mêvan dengê xwe bilind kir û got: "Ma ev Gurî çi kes e?"
1067. In the gathering the guest youth raised his voice and said: "After all what person is this Gurî?"

1068. Zerdo: Yabo zilamekî mehe ye wilo ye, û ketîye xeta xerabîyê.
1068. Zerdo: Father, he is a man of ours (our relative) it is like that, and he has fallen into the line of badness.

1069. Mêvan: Kuro wele dema nîvro ez hatim yekî gurî û çepel li bin darekê rûniştibû, kenikê serê xwe dixurandin, gelo ne ew Gurîyê we ye?
1069. Guest: Boy by God at noon time I came a scabby and filthy one had sat under a tree, scratching the sores of his head, I wonder is that not your Gurî?

1070. Civat: belê belê wele ew e, Gurîyê qedê.
1070. The gathering: yes yes by God it is him, Gurî of the calamity.

1071. Mêvan: De hema sibe ez ê rabim herim rişma mihîna xwe di qirikê xim û ji we re bînim, hûn wî girê didin, dikujin, bi kêfa we ye.
1071. Guest: Then just tomorrow I will get up and go put the halter of my mare on his throat and bring him to you, you tie him, kill him, it is by your pleasure.

1072. Civat: Wele tu wilo bike, em ê te hilgirin û dergîsîya te jî bidin te.
1072. The gathering: By God you do so, we will elevate you and give your fiancée to you too.

1073. Mêvan mêriko bi dergîsî ye, dil bi xwe ve ye, got: "Qey li min nabe sibe?"
1073. The guest, the man is with fiancée, he is pleased with himself, said: "Will tomorrow never come for me?" (Literally: Does it not become tomorrow for me?)

1074. Civat belav bû, gundî her yek çûn malê xwe, bi kêf in, wê Gurî sibe bigirin û bikin Qirdikê Qidoş û li nav gund bigerînin û heyfa gundîya û çêlek û bizina, ker û qantira û darê reza jê hilînin.
1074. The gathering scattered, the villagers each went to their home, they are with joy, they will catch Gurî tomorrow and make him Qirdikê Qidoş (a mocked clown) and walk him around the village and exact the revenge of the villagers and cows and goats, donkeys and mules and trees of the vineyards from him.

1075. Serê sibê zû bi rohilat ve, gundîya girte ser mala xezûrê mêvanê do.
1075. Early in the morning with the sunrise, the villagers closed in on the house of the father-in-law of yesterday's guest.

1076. Mêvanê xort ji xew rakirin û jê re gotin,
1076. They woke the guest youth from sleep and said to him,

1077. "ha pismam, tu xwedîyê zirtê xwe yê şevê dî yî? rabe here wî werîne, heger rast e ne derew e".
1077. "ah cousin, are you the owner of your boast of last night? get up and go bring him, if it is truth and not a lie".

1078. Mêvan: Dil bi xwe ve ye, dergîsîya wî li hundir e, deng dibihîze, mêriko li xwe danayine bê ez naçim, yan ez newêrim, ji dergisiya xwe fedî dike.
1078. Guest: He is pleased with himself, his fiancée is inside, she hears the voice, the man does not put it on himself (cannot bear) to say I am not going, or I do not dare, he feels ashamed before his fiancée.

1079. Hema rabû cilê xwe li xwe kirin û xurcezîna mihîna xwe lê şidand û nigê xwe xiste zenguyê û siwar bû berê xwe da Gurî.
1079. He just got up and put his clothes on himself and tightened the saddlebags of his mare on her and put his foot in the stirrup and mounted and turned his direction to Gurî.

1080. Gundî jî giş li ber dîwaran, li ser sergoyan kom bûne li hêvîya siwar û Gurî ne.
1080. The villagers too all have gathered before the walls, on the dung heaps and are waiting for the rider and Gurî.

1081. Mêvan (siwar) giha cem Gurî, bang kirîyê û got: "Gurî, Gurî! Ez ji te re dibêjim were bi min re".
1081. The guest (rider) reached Gurî, called to him and said: "Gurî, Gurî! I say to you come with me".

1082. Guri: Çima kuro?
1082. Gurî: Why boy?

1083. Ez ê bi te re bêm ku derê?"
1083. Where will I come with you?"

1084. Siwar: Were bi min re, em ê herin gund.
1084. Rider: Come with me, we will go to the village.

1085. Gurî: Gundê li ku lo, min bigirin, wê min
1085. Gurî: Village of where boy, if they catch me, they will

1086. bikujin.
1086. kill me.

1087. Siwar: Mane di heqê te de ye, te dewar û pezê wan giş kur û kem û bêterî kirine.
1087. Rider: For it is in your right (you deserve it), you have made their cattle and sheep all clipped and lacking and tailless.

1088. Gurî: Ma a te çi ye law, de ji vir here, berî ez çiplaqekî bi te vekim.
1088. Gurî: What business is yours boy, come go from here, before I attach (strike) a sharp dagger upon you.

1089. Siwar: Biner Gurî ku ez dakevim, ez ê sîlakê bi te vekim diranên te bişkînim.
1089. Rider: Look Gurî if I come down, I will attach a slap on you and break your teeth.

1090. Gurî: Kuro ji vir here law, qey xwîna te ketîye çavê te?
1090. Gurî: Boy go from here boy, has your blood fallen into your eye?

1091. Siwar bi hêrs peya bû û destê xwe avêt Gurî ku sîlakê lê xîne, hema Gurî bi zîlana qirkê girt û çîplaqek li newqê xist, da erdê.
1091. The rider with anger dismounted and threw his hand at Gurî to strike him with a slap, Gurî just grabbed him by the vein of the throat and struck a sharp dagger to his waist, threw him to the ground.

1092. Mêrik ne îro mirîye, îro deh ro mirîye.
1092. The man has not died today, he has died ten days today.

1093. Bînçikandî, kefê di dev re avêt, çavên zerdoq di nava serî de dilîstin.
1093. Breath-choked, he threw foam from the mouth, his yellow eyes were playing (rolling) inside his head.

1094. Gurî di ser re sekinî û lê nerî û got: "Kuro ev tu ne siwarê do bû?"
1094. Gurî stopped above him and looked at him and said: "Boy were you not the rider of yesterday?"

1095. Siwar: Belê wele ez bûm.
1095. Rider: Yes by God it was me.

1096. Guri: Çi bela te ye pismam?
1096. Gurî: What is your calamity cousin?

1097. Ma çi îşê te ji min heye?
1097. After all what business do you have with me?

1098. Siwar: Wele do ez li mala dergîsîya xwe bûm, em çûn odeyê, gotin û çîrokê gundîya giş li ser te û finasê te bûn, min
1098. Rider: By God yesterday I was at my fiancée's house, we went to the room, the sayings and stories of the villagers were all upon you and your trickery, I

1099. jî ji xwe re zirtek kir û min got, ez ê sibe herim Gurî ji we re bînim û hefsarê mihîna xwe têxim qirkê û bînim ber destê we.
1099. too made a boast for myself and I said, tomorrow I will go bring Gurî to you and put the halter of my mare on his throat and bring him before your hands.

1100. Gurî: Biner pismam ji bo xatirê zirta te ez ê bi te re bêm û bera kêfa dergîsîya te bê û nav di te bide û ji te re bilîlîne, lê biner law gundê Silîvanîyê kes nikare îşê xwe ji min bîne, yan li mi xe, min bikuje, ji apê min pê ve, heger tê soz bi min re bide, ez ê bi te re bêm û heger tu nedî, ez nayêm.
1100. Gurî: Look cousin for the sake of your boast I will come with you and let your fiancée's joy come and give you a name (praise you) and trill for you, but look boy the village of Silîva no one can bring their business from me (defeat me), or strike me, kill me, other than my uncle, if you will give a promise with me, I will come with you and if you do not give, I am not coming.

1101. Siwar: Sozê çi?
1101. Rider: Promise of what?

1102. Tu çi soz û peymanê ji min bixwaze, ez ê bi cih bînim, hema tu min fedîkar nekî li pêşîya gundîya û mala xezûrê min, û li pêş dergîsîya min, ka tu çi dibêjî, bibêje.
1102. Whatever promise and pact you want from me, I will bring to place (fulfill), just you do not make me ashamed before the villagers and my father-in-law's house, and before my fiancée, well what do you say, say it.

1103. Gurî: Ez ê rişma mihîna te têxim hustê xwe û ez ê bidim dû te wek hêsîra, lê biner law gava min got, min berde, tê min berdî, yan ez heyvanê rih bi te ve nahêlim, û sed sal derbas bibin, heya ez sax im ez nahêlim tu ji gund derkeve.
1103. Gurî: I will put the halter of your mare on my neck and I will go behind you like captives, but look boy when I said, release me, you will release me, or I will not leave the animal of a soul attached to you, and a hundred years may pass, as long as I am alive I will not let you go out of the village.

1104. Siwar: Na na ji bo Xwedê, hema tu bêje min berde ez ê te berdim.
1104. Rider: No no for God's sake, just you say release me I will release you.

1105. Gurî: De xem nake, de ka rişma mihîna te.
1105. Gurî: Then it makes no worry, then let us have the halter of your mare.

1106. Û wek şivqaskê (devgavkê) xiste hustê xwe de û da dû siwar û berê xwe bi hev re dan gund.
1106. And like a muzzle (gag) he put it on his neck and went behind the rider and together they turned their direction to the village.

1107. Gundî giş derketine ser bêndera, ber dîwara, mêr û jin û zarok bi kêf û şahî, û lîlelîla pîreka ye.
1107. The villagers all have gone out onto the threshing floors, before the walls, men and women and children with joy and celebration, and it is the trilling of the females.

1108. Silo: Kuro wa bira mêrik Gurî anî law!
1108. Silo: Boy look brother the man brought Gurî boy!

1109. Simo: Bê henek lo, ka çavên min gelekî nabînin.
1109. Simo: Without joke boy, for my eyes do not see much.

1110. Şero: Ha wa bi dû de ye, wele bi rişma mihînê girêdaye.
1110. Şero: Ah look he is behind, by God he is tied with the mare's halter.

1111. Zerdo: Apê Gurî de binerin gundîno, alîkarîya min bikin, hema ez karibim wî qeyd û merbet û bend bikim.
1111. Zerdo: Gurî's uncle, then look villagers, do my help, so that I can just fetter and tether and bind him.

1112. Şerefo: Kuro hayê we jê hebe, ji nav destê we nefilite ha.
1112. Şerefo: Boy have your awareness of him, let him not escape from your hands ah.

1113. Sîno: Na na nafilite, mane em komek zilam in û ew yekî tenê ye.
1113. Sîno: No no he does not escape, for we are a group of men and he is a single one.

1114. Şerefo: De min ji we re negot, niha hûn ê hunerê Gurî bibînin bê çawa wek pêlewana xwe ji nav we xelas bike.
1114. Şerefo: Then did I not say to you, now you will see Gurî's skill how like champions he frees himself from among you.

1115. Bi qîreqîr û carecar û barebara zarokan û lîlelîlê pîrekan, siwar û Gurî bi dû de gihan ser bênderan.
1115. With the shouting and clamor and bleating of the children and the trilling of the females, the rider and Gurî behind him reached upon the threshing floors.

1116. Guri wa nerî ku apê wî çokîdara xistiye bin çengê xwe de û çawa kevira û erdê jê didize û hêdî hêdî di nav zilaman re xwe dide pêş.
1116. Gurî there looked that his uncle has put a heavy stick under his armpit and how he steals stones and ground from him (sneaks up) and slowly puts himself forward among the men.

1117. Gurî got: "Wa siwaro law, min berde, wa apê min hat".
1117. Gurî said: "Hey rider boy, release me, hey my uncle has come".

1118. Siwar: Te berdim, çilo kuro?
1118. Rider: Release you, how boy?

1119. Wele felek bavê te be ez te bernadim.
1119. By God even if fate is your father I am not releasing you.

1120. Gurî: Hêêê... siwaro bêbexto, ka ew soza te dabû min li çolê.
1120. Gurî: Heee... luckless rider, where is that promise you had given me in the wilderness.

1121. Siwar: De bila qirara soza Xwedê li min ketibe ku ez bihêlim tu derkevî ji gundê Silîvanîyê.
1121. Rider: Then let the decision of God's promise have fallen upon me if I let you go out of the village of Silîva.

1122. Di gavê de hatibû bîra Gurî ku sîxîka kêrê ji ber xwe derxistibû û dabû ser rişmê, û bi zîlana kêrê rişme qetand û revîya û kete qûntara çîyê.
1122. In the moment it had come to Gurî's mind that he had taken out the blade of the knife from his side and had put it on the halter, and with the sharp edge of the knife cut the halter and fled and fell to the foot of the mountain.

1123. Zarok û sîpa dabûn dû li wan vegerîya û bi lepê kevira giş xistin gundê Silîvanîyê û bang kir, "ho siwaro bêbexto ma ez nema dihêlim tu ji gund derkeve, ma ez rih bi te ve berdidim".
1123. The children and youths had fallen behind him, he returned upon them and with handfuls of stones struck all of them into the village of Silîva and called out, "ho luckless rider for I no longer let you go out of the village, for do I leave a soul attached to you".

1124. Revîya ser çîyê, gundî vegerîyan malên xwe û her yek ji xwe re tiştekî dibêje.
1124. He fled to the mountain, the villagers returned to their homes and each says something to himself.

1125. Li Gurî bû şev ji kevirekî diçe ser kevirekî, ji hîmekî diçe ser latekî, ji darekê diçe bin darekê heya ji gund bi dûr ket.
1125. Night fell on Gurî, from a stone he goes onto a stone, from a foundation stone he goes onto a rock, from a tree he goes under a tree until he fell far from the village.

1126. Li ser latekê palda û di dilê xwe de dibêje, "xelkê Silîva bila we çikiribe, ma ji nûv re ez dihêlim pez û dewarên we li van topraxa biçêrin, ma heya a xerab hebe ez nakim a çê".
1126. He leaned back on a rock and in his heart he says, "people of Silîva let whatever you have done, for anew will I let your sheep and cattle graze on these lands, for as long as the bad exists I do not do the good".

1127. Û bû keleş û çete û kete dora gund, nema dihêle ne kes here derekê, aşekî, bajarekî û nema dihêle kes bê gund.
1127. And he became a brigand and bandit and fell around the village, he no longer lets neither anyone go somewhere, to a mill, to a city and no longer lets anyone come to the village.

1128. Bi vî hali gund û Gurî man li ber hev.
1128. In this state the village and Gurî remained facing each other.

1129. Demek derbas bû, piştî çend rojan, hefteyekê, mehekê,gundî ketine qelaqê de û nema zanin wê çi bikin.
1129. A time passed, after a few days, a week, a month, the villagers fell into agitation and no longer know what they will do.

1130. Gurî jî bi şev li bin darekê paldaye û bi ser halê xwe û feqîrîya xwe de dipojine û di dilê xwe de dibêje, "wilo çênabe, ne kes, ne kus, ne mal, ne xanî, ma ez cenawer im, ma ez hov
1130. Gurî too at night has leaned back under a tree and ponders upon his state and his poverty and in his heart he says, "it does not work like this, no person, no kin, no house, no home, am I a beast, am I wild

1131. im?
1131. ?

1132. Ez li çol û pola bi şev û bi roj bi tena xwe, ne nan, ne xwarin, ne cil, ne şûştin.
1132. I in the wildernesses and plains by night and by day by myself, no bread, no food, no clothes, no washing.

1133. Wê havîn bê, çile bê, germa havînê li bin dara naqede û serma zivistanê tew naqede li vê çolê".
1133. Summer will come, winter will come, the heat of summer does not finish under the trees and the cold of winter absolutely does not finish in this wilderness".

1134. Ji xwe re mitale dike û dipojine û berdewam dike û dibêje, "ma cîyê min li vi gundî, li vî warî heye?
1134. He deliberates for himself and ponders and continues and says, "after all does my place exist in this village, in this domain?

1135. Ku ez xwe li vir bidim erdê wê kî parîk nan bide min, firek av?
1135. If I throw myself to the ground here who will give me a piece of bread, a splash of water?

1136. A baş ew e ku ez ji vî welatî, ji vê herêmê, ji vê derebegîyê tevdî derkevim û herim cihekî din, welatekî din.
1136. The good thing is that I completely go out from this country, from this region, from this principality and go to another place, another country.

1137. Dunya mezin û fire ye, ma qene ez ê li nanê xwe bimînim heyîrî, rizq li Xwedê ye".
1137. The world is great and wide, after all will I remain bewildered over my bread, sustenance is upon God".

1138. Û hêdî hêdî xilmaş bû û di xew ve çû.
1138. And slowly he dozed off and went to sleep.

1139. Ji nişkê ve çeng dibe, ji xew şîyar dibe, ew bi xwe serî dagirtîye ji ramanan û ji kar û finasa, ji tîna û ji birçîna.
1139. Suddenly he jerks up, he wakes from sleep, he himself has filled his head with thoughts and with deeds and trickery, from thirst and from hunger.

1140. Careke din serê xwe danî ser destekî xwe û çavên xwe girtin û xwe di xew ve bir, tuxtek çû neçû careke din ji xew veciniqî û şîyar bû, rabû ji cihê xwe û çû li cihekî din palda û got: "Ma qey min li ser mûristana, mîrawa paldaye bavo?!"
1140. Once again he laid his head on his hand and closed his eyes and took himself to sleep, a short while went or not (passed) once again he startled from sleep and woke, he got up from his place and went leaned back in another place and said: "Have I really leaned back upon anthills, ant-nests father?!"

1141. Berî şeveq lê xîne, careke din şîyar bû.
1141. Before the dawn strikes, once again he woke.

1142. Di vir de hinek sawêr û efsane têde heye.
1142. In here there is some vision and myth in it.

1143. Dibêjin, "Xocê Xizir hatîye li pêşîya Gurî spîya sekinîye (wilo hatîye gotin) û jê re gotîye, Siyamed, metirse, ez Xocê Xizir im, rabe ji vir here, ev cih nema ji te re dibe û tu kes zora te nabe bi şûr û mertala, bi gemş û çenga, bi navê û destlepkê, û mirina te li ser himta cenawera ye û tu bi destên kesî ji insanan nayê kuştin".
1143. They say, "Master Khidr has come and stood before Gurî in white (so it has been said) and said to him, Sîyamend, do not fear, I am Master Khidr, get up go from here, this place no longer becomes (is suitable for) you and no one can defeat you with swords and shields, with wrestling and grabbing, with name and hand-grappling, and your death is on the charge of beasts and you will not be killed by the hands of anyone from humans".

1144. Gurî çavên xwe vekirin şeveqê lê xistîye, tayê spî û reş ji hev tên naskirin, li dora xwe nerî tu kes nedît, di dilê xwe de got: "Bavo, ev xewn bû?
1144. Gurî opened his eyes the dawn has struck, the white and black thread are recognized from each other, he looked around him he saw no one, in his heart he said: "Father, was this a dream?

1145. Ev rast bû?
1145. Was this truth?

1146. Ev çi bû?"
1146. What was this?"

1147. Û Gurî bêhnekê ma di cihê xwe de û saw girt û lerizî ji tirsa.
1147. And Gurî remained a moment in his place and took fright and trembled from fear.

1148. Ew bixwe berê ev raman û gotin û paşeroja wî ketibû bîr û bala wî de û wê şevê pê de dida ber hev û dipîva û çep û rast lê dixist, û ji xwe re paşeroj xweş dikir û xwe dikir zilam, xwedî jin û mal û zarok, û di vê heyecana kûr û dirêj de di xew ve çû û xewn dîtin.
1148. He himself before these thoughts and words and his future had fallen into his mind and attention and that night he was comparing them and measuring and striking left and right, and making the future pleasant for himself and making himself a man, owner of a wife and home and children, and in this deep and long excitement he went to sleep and saw dreams.

1149. Hema rabû ser xwe, xwe ji tozê û axê daweşand û çîplaqê xwe xiste ber pişta xwe û tim û tim berjor çû û ji xwe re dibêje, "rizqê min ji vir qutbû, Silîva û xelkê wê ji min re ne dost û
1149. He just got up on himself (stood up), shook himself from dust and earth and put his sharp dagger before his back and always and always went upwards and says to himself, "my sustenance was cut from here, Silîva and its people are not friends and

1150. mirov in, ez ê ji vî welatî herim, xwene rizqê min ma li Silîva?"
1150. relatives for me, I will go from this country, after all did my sustenance remain in Silîva?"

1151. Qunaxek hilanî yek danî, rêwî ye bi nav dar û devîya dikeve û ji xwe re tiştina ji dara jê dike û dixwe, çi fêkîyê li dara ketibe ji birçîna dixwe, diçe ser cok û kanîyên avê xwe diso û xwe tesel dike û têr vedixwe.
1151. He lifted a stage and put down one (traveled stage by stage), he is a traveler he falls among trees and bushes and cuts things from the trees for himself and eats, whatever fruit had fallen on the trees he eats from hunger, he goes onto streams and springs of water he washes himself and comforts himself and drinks to satisfaction.

1152. Û bi vî hawî rêya ber jor girtîye û dimeşe.
1152. And in this manner he has taken the upward road and walks.

1153. Biner bê çend roj çûn û derbas bûn û Gurî daye ser oxira xwe û pişta xwe daye felekê, nizane wê bi ku derê de here, wê berê xwe bi ku de bike, weke dînê biçolaketî lê hatîye.
1153. Look how a few days went and passed and Gurî has set on his journey and has given his back to fate, he does not know where he will go, where he will turn his direction to, it has come upon him like a madman fallen to the wilderness.

1154. Serê sibehekê roj du bejna bilind bûye, Gurî bi rê de dimeşe, bi oxira xwe de carekê dît ku wa rêwîyek weke wî bi rê de ji jor de tê.
1154. One early morning the sun has risen two heights, Gurî walks on the road, on his journey at once he saw that there a traveler like him comes on the road from above.

1155. Gurî di dilê xwe de dibêje, "vaye nêçîra min ji min re hat, ez ê wî tazî bikim cilê wî li xwe bikim û ez ê vê ebê bidimê, wele ez di bin de mirim, bera ew jî çendakî li xwe ke xene wê dunya xerab bibe...", wilo ji xwe re dibêje.
1155. Gurî says in his heart, "here is my prey has come for me, I will strip him naked I will put his clothes on myself and I will give this cloak to him, by God I have died under it, let him too wear it a while otherwise the world will be ruined...", so he says to himself.

1156. Nêzîkayî li hev kirin, silav li hev kirin û li hev pirsîn:
1156. They approached each other, they greeted each other and asked each other:

1157. Guri: Xorto tu ji ku derê tê?
1157. Gurî: Youth where do you come from?

1158. Tê here bi ku derê de?
1158. Where are you going?

1159. Xort (rêwî): Wele ez ji zozana têm, berê min li germîyana ye.
1159. Youth (traveler): By God I come from the high pastures, my direction is to the warm plains.

1160. Guri: Ji zozên, tu ji ku derê yî?
1160. Gurî: From the high pastures, where are you from?

1161. Rêwî: Wele ez ji êl û eşîra Omer Axa me, ez ji wê derê têm.
1161. Traveler: By God I am from the clan and tribe of Omer Axa, I come from there.

1162. Guri: Omer Axa zilamekî çilo ye?
1162. Gurî: What kind of man is Omer Axa?

1163. Çawa ye?
1163. How is he?

1164. Rêwî: Wele Omer Axa zilameki kutek e, bi mal û milk û dewlet e, sî û sê gundê wî hene, di qûntara çîyê de ne, tu kes nikare nigê xwe li nigê wî bixe.
1164. Traveler: By God Omer Axa is a forceful man, he is with wealth and property and fortune, he has thirty-three villages, they are in the foothills of the mountain, no one can put his foot against his foot (match him).

1165. Gurî: Pismam tu nayê em bi hev re bazarekê bikin.
1165. Gurî: Cousin will you not come we make a bargain with each other.

1166. Rêwî: Bazara çi yabo, ma çîyê me di ber hev de heye?
1166. Traveler: Bargain of what father, after all what of ours exists before each other?

1167. Ez rêwî me û tu rêwî ye, em ê her yek bi ser oxira xwe de herin û hew, ma me malê hev xwarîye?
1167. I am a traveler and you are a traveler, we will each go upon our journey and that is all, after all have we eaten each other's wealth?

1168. Min sînorê te qulaptîye li em li ser bazarê bikin?"
1168. Have I overturned your border that we should make a bargain over it?"

1169. Guri: Wele bira erê em her du rêwî ne, lê rêya me ne yek e, tu ji zozana tê, tê herî germîyana, û ez ji germîyana têm, ez ê herim zozana.
1169. Gurî: By God brother yes we are both travelers, but our road is not one, you come from the high pastures, you will go to the warm plains, and I come from the warm plains, I will go to the high pastures.

1170. Zozan sar û berf û baran e, û germîyan hênik
1170. The high pastures are cold and snow and rain, and the warm plains are cool

1171. û ro û sayî ye, xweş e.
1171. and sun and clear skies, it is pleasant.

1172. Van cilê xwe bide min û ez ê jî vê ebê bidim te, tê here germîyana, ne xema te ye, lê yê min ez ê herim zozana, sar û qefalî ye.
1172. Give these clothes of yours to me and I too will give this cloak to you, you will go to the warm plains, it is not your worry, but as for me I will go to the high pastures, it is cold and freezing.

1173. Rêwî wilo lê nerî, li rû û mûçikê kiretî nerî, serê gurî, giş kenik, eba qetîyayî giş pîne, qilêra pê ve, spî wilo jê digindirin û dikevin erdê, û got: "Biner Gurî, ez sewtakê li te xim, ez ê te gêj bikim û te bigindirînim newalê ha, tu dîn e?
1173. The traveler looked at him thus, looked at the ugly face and features, the scabby head, all sores, the torn cloak all patches, the dirt on it, the lice rolling off him like that and falling to the ground, and said: "Look Gurî, if I strike a blow to you, I will make you dizzy and roll you down the valley ah, are you mad?

1174. Tu hov e?
1174. Are you wild?

1175. Çilo ez ê cilê xwe yê nû û paqij bidim bi vê eba kevnik û pertî û tije spî, qey tu dîn bûye law?"
1175. How will I give my new and clean clothes for this old and tattered cloak full of lice, have you gone mad boy?"

1176. Gurî: Biner biner şitexalîya zêde ji kêm qilî ye, ê min bi xwe ez ê cilê te bistînim û li xwe bikim, tu ê min li xwe dike, nake tu bi kêfa xwe ye.
1176. Gurî: Look look excess talking is from lack of sense, as for me myself I will take your clothes and wear them, whether you wear mine or do not wear them it is by your pleasure.

1177. Yek ji Gurî yek ji xortê rêwî, gotinê wan bi ber hev de hatin.
1177. One from Gurî one from the traveler youth, their words came before each other (they exchanged words).

1178. Xortê rêwî li xwe nerî, li Gruî nerî û got: "Ya Rebî, ya Xwedêyo, ev çi bela bû te anîbû pêşîya min?"
1178. The traveler youth looked at himself, looked at Gurî and said: "O Lord, o God, what calamity was this you had brought before me?"

1179. Û destê xwe hilda ku sewtakê li rûçkê Gurî xe, Gurî xwe ji ber da alîyekî û hencika hestê wî girt û çiplaqek li newqê xist.
1179. And he raised his hand to strike a blow to Gurî's face, Gurî put himself aside from before him and grabbed his elbow joint and struck a sharp dagger to his waist.

1180. Pepûkê rêwî bê hiş kete erdê, hema Gurî eba xwe ji xwe danî avêt wê navê û bi lez cilê wî pepûkî jê kirin û li xwe kirin û jê re got: "Birak ê min bixwe va min cilê te li xwe kirin, birin û ez ji te re nabêjim eba min li xwe ke, ya li xwe neke, tu bi kêfa xwe yî, û va ez çûm", û da ser rê lezand û çû.
1180. The poor traveler fell to the ground without consciousness, Gurî just took his cloak off himself threw it there and with speed took off that poor one's clothes and put them on himself and said to him: "Brother as for myself look I put your clothes on myself, I took them and I do not say to you wear my cloak, or do not wear it, you are by your pleasure, and look I have gone", and set on the road sped up and went.

1181. Qûnaxek hilanî û yek danî, mêrko cilê wî nih in, paqij in, bi kêf û peye ye.
1181. He lifted a stage and put down one, the little man his clothes are new, they are clean, he is with joy and firm on his feet.

1182. Nêzîkayî li gundê Omer Axa kir, giha şivana, gavana, dipirse, ev çi gund e?
1182. He approached the village of Omer Axa, he reached the shepherds, the herdsmen, he asks, what village is this?

1183. Bi pirsa, Gurî xwe gihand gundê Omer Axa, lê bi ser gund ve qulipî, heydê çi gundekî mezin û bela wela hawîrdora gund bexçe û dar û devî ne, di orta gund de ji alîyê bakur ve maleke mezin û holîke bilind di ser re û li başûrî malê (kuşkê) hewşeke mezin û fireh li pêşîyê ye, û di kêleka malê qesrek mezin û bilind, ode û dîwana Omer Begê ye û cihê civata gundîyan û şevbihêrka zilamê gund û mêvanê Omer Begê ye.
1183. With questioning, Gurî reached himself to the village of Omer Axa, but he spilled over the village, heydee what a great and scattered village the surroundings of the village are gardens and trees and bushes, in the middle of the village from the north side a great house and a high hall above it and to the south of the house (mansion) a great and wide courtyard is before it, and beside the house a great and high palace, it is the room and court of Omer Beg and it is the place of the gathering of the villagers and the evening gathering of the men of the village and the guests of Omer Beg.

1184. Gurî berê xwe da odeya mezin piştî nîvroyê ye û berî êvarî ye.
1184. Gurî turned his direction to the great room it is after noon and before evening.

1185. Derbasî odeyê bû, heydê li civata rûniştî ji gundîyan û bîyanîyan û gundên derdora wî, Gurî jî li kêleka dîwarekî rûnişt wek vanê rûniştî, betilî ye, xilmaş bû ye.
1185. He passed into the room, heydee at the seated gathering of the villagers and strangers and his surrounding villages, Gurî too sat beside a wall like those seated, he is tired, he dozed off.

1186. Nebû yekî ji xulaman dey lê kir: "Gurî, Gurî, rabe şîvê bixwe".
1186. It was not long before one of the servants called to him: "Gurî, Gurî, get up eat dinner".

1187. Pepûkê Gurî xerîbe kesî nas nake, piştî xwarina mêvan û gundîyan, xwarin jê re anîn danî ber.
1187. Poor Gurî is a stranger he recognizes no one, after the food of the guests and villagers, they brought food for him and placed it before him.

1188. Gurîyê reben birçî ye, ji nêza ketîye, zikê xwe ji wan kurtêl û avdonkê dagirt û xwe berda hundirê qehwexaneyê, kurtanek xiste bin serê xwe de û kete xew û bû xirexira wî, zik têr e û hundir germ e; nigê xwe rada xwe kire pîj û ma di xewa şêrîn de heya sibê.
1188. Wretched Gurî is hungry, he has fallen from hunger, he filled his belly with those leftovers and broth and let himself down inside the coffee house, he put a packsaddle under his head and fell to sleep and it became his snoring, the belly is full and the inside is warm; he stretched his legs and made himself straight and remained in sweet sleep until morning.

1189. Gurî bi vî halî ma mêvanê odeya Omer Begê, gundî û xulam û navmalî giş ji Gurî dagirtî ne û li rûçikê wî dinerin, jê toq dibin.
1189. Gurî in this state remained the guest of Omer Beg's room, the villagers and servants and household are all full of (fed up with) Gurî and look at his face, they are repulsed by him.

1190. Gurî kinikê genî, madtehl, rûkirêt, tu naxwaze li dêmê wî binere, wek zebenîyekî ye.
1190. Gurî of foul sores, bitter-mooded, ugly-faced, you do not want to look at his countenance, he is like a demon.

1191. Çendakî wilo ma, mehek dido qedîyan, Gurî bala xwe da xulamê odeyê, gi çi parîk nanê şewitî, qeşmüşk girtî, hestîyê rût û mijandî û pirka ava şûna desta tîne û datîne ber Gurî, carek,dido, sisê.
1191. He remained like that for a while, a month or two finished, Gurî gave his attention to the servant of the room, that whatever piece of burnt bread, mold-caught, bare and sucked bones and the splash of water from hand-washing he brings and puts before Gurî, once, twice, three times.

1192. Gurî nas kir ku ji qazîv ve wilo dike, êvarekê piştî şîvê, Gurî di dilê xwe de got: "Qey ez ne Siyamed im bavo, ma namûs jî nema, wele ev ji qazîv ve wilo dike, de îşev ez jê re zanim".
1192. Gurî recognized that he does so on purpose, one evening after dinner, Gurî said in his heart: "Am I not Sîyamend father, after all did honor no longer remain, by God he does so on purpose, then tonight I know for him (I will teach him a lesson)".

1193. Dema yê xulam careke din nanê şewitî û hestîyê rût danîn ber, hema Gurî rahişt kelhûbekî hestîya û heya Xwedê huner dayê di textikê enîya xulam de lê xist, nehişt av bigihê ser, hum û gum li odeyê ket, hin dibêjin kuşt, hin dibêjin bê henek!
1193. When the servant once again placed the burnt bread and bare bones before him, Gurî just picked up a joint of the bones and as much as God gave him skill he struck it on the board of the servant's forehead, he did not let water reach his head (killed him instantly), hubbub fell in the room, some say he killed him, some say no joke!

1194. Deng û qerbalix giha Omer Begê.
1194. The voice and clamor reached Omer Beg.

1195. Omer Begê: Wî bigirin, wî bernedin, bînin ber destê min, nehêlin bireve.
1195. Omer Beg: Catch him, do not release him, bring him before my hand, do not let him flee.

1196. Gurî: Na na ez narevim, dengê te tê min.
1196. Gurî: No no I do not flee, your voice comes to me.

1197. Çend xort pê ve rabûn ku wî bigirin û bînin ji Omer Begê re, xwe ji nav lepên wan derxist û hat li pêşîya Omer Begê sekinî, û got:
1197. A few youths rose upon him to catch him and bring him for Omer Beg, he extracted himself from among their palms (grasps) and came and stood before Omer Beg, and said:

1198. Gurî: Begê min, axê min, ma ne heqî heye?
1198. Gurî: My beg, my agha, after all is there not a right (justice)?

1199. Heger gunehê min hebe min girê de, min têxe zindanê, min bikuje.
1199. If my sin exists tie me, put me into prison, kill me.

1200. Omer Begê: Law Gurî ka bibêje, çima te ev xulamê reben kuşt?
1200. Omer Beg: Boy Gurî well say, why did you kill this wretched servant?

1201. Gurî: Begê min ev mehek dido ne ku ez mêvanê oda te me û ez zilamekî rêwî me, bêkes û bêxwedî me.
1201. Gurî: My beg it has been a month or two that I am the guest of your room and I am a traveler man, I am without anyone and without an owner.

1202. Xulamê te ji qazîv ve, çi nanê hişk û şewitî û hestîyê rût heye wê deyne ber min û ê din ji xwe re dibe, ma ev qas xelk nanê te dixwin, ez jî yek ji wa me, ne malê wî ye û ne nanê wî ye û ne jina wî çêdike.
1202. Your servant on purpose, whatever dry and burnt bread and bare bones there are he will place before me and takes the rest for himself, after all this many people eat your bread, I too am one of them, it is not his wealth and it is not his bread and his wife does not make it.

1203. Ez qudûmşikenandî bûme, ez nema karim bimeşim, xwe bi qûnaxek divê bighînim ya na, ana ez ji cem te çûbama, cehemî bûma, wele namûsa min ji min re got, wî bikuje, di heqê wî de ye.
1203. I have become broken-bodied, I can no longer walk, I must reach myself a stage or not, otherwise I would have gone from you, I would have gone to hell (disappeared), by God my honor said to me, kill him, it is in his right.

1204. Omer Begê: Gurî law, madam ji bo gepa nanê xwe te ew kuştîye, û birastî jî ne ji heqê wî bû ku nan û xwarinê nede te, ne ji kîsî wî ye.
1204. Omer Beg: Gurî boy, since for your bite of bread you killed him, and in truth too it was not from his right that he does not give bread and food to you, it is not from his pocket.

1205. Wele Gurî ez te di odeya xwe de pîs nakim, te nakujim.
1205. By God Gurî I do not dirty you in my room, I do not kill you.

1206. Xêr pir e, bux û vexwe, rizq li Xwedê ye.
1206. Charity is abundant, eat and drink, sustenance is upon God.

1207. Gurî ma bi kêfa xwe li odeyê.
1207. Gurî remained by his pleasure in the room.

1208. Ehmeqê qehweçî jî karê wî ji pirka binê misîn, telpa binê fincanê heye, dide dest Gurî, ne carek, ne dido û ne sisê.
1208. The fool coffee-maker too his work is that whatever dregs of the bottom of the pitcher, grounds of the bottom of the cup there are, he gives to Gurî's hand, not once, not twice and not three times.

1209. Gurî di dilê xwe de got: "Ez ji vîr jî zanim, ez ê wî jî bikujim".
1209. Gurî said in his heart: "I know for this one too, I will kill him too".

1210. Şevekê qehweçî telpa binê misîn û fincana da dest Gurî, Gurî hema fincan zîzikand û di textikê enîya wî de lê xist, ew zîz kir erdê ew jî kuşt, deng çû bi Omer Begê ve.
1210. One night the coffee-maker gave the grounds of the bottom of the pitcher and cups to Gurî's hand, Gurî just whizzed the cup and struck it on the board of his forehead, he dropped him whizzing to the ground he killed him too, the voice went to Omer Beg.

1211. Omer Begê: Kuro Gurî, ev çi bela te ye law?
1211. Omer Beg: Boy Gurî, what calamity of yours is this boy?

1212. Gurî: Ezbenî wele karê wî jî, pirka binê misîna û telpa binê fencana dixist ser hev û dida min, ma qene qehwa te ji kîsî bavê wî ye?
1212. Gurî: Sir by God his work too, he was putting the dregs of the bottom of pitchers and the grounds of the bottom of cups upon each other and giving them to me, after all is your coffee from his father's pocket?

1213. Xelk û mêvan û rêwî û gundî giş vedixwin, ez jî yek ji wa me.
1213. People and guests and travelers and villagers all drink, I too am one of them.

1214. Omer Begê: Gurî law, wilo çênabe, ji xwe re karekî bike, ka bêje bê çi kar ji te tê?
1214. Omer Beg: Gurî boy, it does not work like this, do a work for yourself, well say what work comes from you?

1215. Gurî: Begê min wele hemî kar ji min tên.
1215. Gurî: My beg by God all works come from me.

1216. Omer Begê: Ez ê karekî sivik bidim te.
1216. Omer Beg: I will give a light work to you.

1217. Guri: Wek çi karî?
1217. Gurî: Like what work?

1218. Omer Begê: Hema mêvanek hat odê, tê rabe tasek av bidîyê û rûnê.
1218. Omer Beg: Just a guest came to the room, you will get up and give a bowl of water to him and sit.

1219. Guri: Wele begê min ez nikarim wek sing li ber derî rawestim, mêvanên te yek tê û yek dire, havîn e, zivistan tê sar e, ez vî karî nakim.
1219. Gurî: By God my beg I cannot stand like a peg before the door, your guests one comes and one goes, it is summer, winter comes it is cold, I do not do this work.

1220. Omer Begê: Nexwe tu kar ji te nayê?
1220. Omer Beg: So no work comes from you?

1221. Gurî: Ezbenî, wele tu bê çi kar ji min tê.
1221. Gurî: Sir, by God you say what work comes from me.

1222. Omer Beg: Aniha ma tu nikarî hema mêvanek hat, hespê wî ji dest bigirî û bavê şerîta tewlê?
1222. Omer Beg: Now can you not just a guest came, take his horse by the hand and throw him to the rope of the stable?

1223. Gurî: Ezbenî, wele ev kar jî ji min nayê, mêvanê te deh dirin û deh tên, ji min nayê.
1223. Gurî: Sir, by God this work too does not come from me, your guests ten go and ten come, it does not come from me.

1224. Omer Begê: Naxwe tu kar ji te nayê?
1224. Omer Beg: So no work comes from you?

1225. Gurî: Ezbeni wele hemû kar ji min tên.
1225. Gurî: Sir by God all works come from me.

1226. Omer Begê: Aniha tu û karê alîyê malê çawa ne?
1226. Omer Beg: Now you and the work of the house's side how are they?

1227. Hema tiştek lazim bû tê here bîne û bê.
1227. Just a thing was necessary you will go bring it and come.

1228. Gurî: Ezbenî, wele ez ji mortemorta pîreka gelekî aciz im, ez naxwazim tu wî karî jî bi min bike.
1228. Gurî: Sir, by God I am very annoyed by the muttering of the women, I do not want you to make me do that work either.

1229. Omer Begê: Madem wilo ye, ez ê karekî rihet û sivik bidim ber te.
